O, sons, because I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by its fulfillment, its end is achieved in it, and by its expositions and by its declarations, it is my view that you complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the operation with my hand, that is, surgery.
Because the operation with the hand is laid low in our region and in our time completely private, while it is greatly perilous the science of it, and its knowledge is held hostage; and there remain of it only a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered and become subject to those errors and misunderstandings, because the clauses of it are understood and the strength of it and the art are elongated.
And it is seen to me that you vivify that with the ordering of this treatise in that according to the way of exposition and of declaration and of abbreviation; and for that it may come with the forms of the tools of cautery and of the other instruments of the work as it is for the addition of the declaration, and for the preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which no good artificer with his hand is found in this our time, is because the art of medicine is long, and that it behoves the actor of it to be exercised before that in the science of anatomy, which reconciles Gualia in that it knows the joints of the members and the forms of those, and the conjunction and the separation of them; and he has the knowledge of the bones, of the nerves and of the vessels, and the number of those, and the egress of them; and of the pulsating veins and of the quiet ones, and of the places of the emission of them.
And for that, it is said by Hippocrates that with a name it is little, but in the work great, and most of all in the art of the hand.
But we have already said of that in the introduction of this book; for who is not learned in that which we have said of anatomy, is not evacuated that he will not fall into error for which many men die, thus as I have seen too many of those, who some are formed in this science and cast themselves from that their science and their experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced physician who had incised an abscess scrophilos in the neck of a woman, and incised some arteries of the neck for which flowed great blood while the woman died among the hands of him.
And I saw another physician who prescribed that the trachea of a man who had processed in his state, and the stone was great, and it came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, for that man on the third day died.
And I had already been called to extract that, and I saw that by the greatness of the stone and by the disposition of the patient I knew above him that he would die.
And I saw another physician who took a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he was given a black cravat who was broken in the thigh of him; and prepared the physician with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, above the wound, with splints and splints with strong structure, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
And then he dismissed him according to his desires, and he bound him, and he left him for some days and commanded that we untie the ligament; and thus it was that the thigh and the foot became infected, and he came to perdition.
And I was called to him, and I appeared to untie the ligament, and achieved tranquility and then eased his pains.
But however, already corruption was confirmed in the limb, for that I could not restrain it, and it did not cease to wander the corruption in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated after some days, until the malignancy of it was magnified to his lord.
The cause is that the cancer is pure of melancholic humor, therefore it behoves that it may not come to it with iron of all, but that it be in a member the which suffers that of all it be held hostage.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary to you that the operation with the hand be devised in two divisions: that is in operation to that which is associated with health, and in work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already existed that in all places of this book in which I come operation in which there is error and fear; for it is necessary to you that you guard this and leave that, so that the foolish do not attain a way to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore take your arms with solicitude and with the protection of God, and your patients with facility and with firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God, pursuing health and laudable success, and leave the maladies terrible of difficult healing, and hold your arms from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not escape you: for more it remains to your glory, and more in the world and in the end to your sanctities.
Gualia has already said in some of his admonitions: "Do not meddle with bad malady, so that bad physicians you not be called."
And I have already divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and the first of the first part. The first chapter ordered of the head within feet, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of what is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of suction and perforation, and of leeches, and of poultices, and of the extraction of arrows and of things similar to them, all chaptered and ordered of the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and dislocation, and of the cure of sprains and of things similar to them; chapter ordered of the head within feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Know that you should say the quality of the judgments of that cautery and of its inconveniences, and in what completion it should be prohibited cautery.
Therefore I say that the sermon of the quality of the judgment of cautery and of its inconvenience is a long and prolix sermon, and subtle by science, and secret hidden; and already of it has spoken a great multitude of wise men, and of it they have disagreed, and to me suffices a little of the sermons of theirs, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cautery conforms to every completion universally which is in matter or has matter, except for two complections, which are complections caused by its matter.
In the completion caused and dry with matter they disagree; for some say that cautery is beneficial to that, and others say the contrary of that, that cautery is not convenient in illness which is by quality and by dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and inconvenient is that illness caused and dry with that which is caut and dry be healed.
And say that one who says the contrary of that, that by cautery is made benefit in all illness caused and dry which comes in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and its humidities to the completion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say for the sermon of that, that experience this already to me some times has discovered.
But however, it does not behoove that it comes upon this one who already is experienced and exercised in the chapter of cautery by previous exercise, and has known the diversity of the complexion of men and the disposition of the illnesses in their own bodies, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the space of time of those.
But in the other complections, there is no fear upon you, and more so in the illnesses cold and humid, because already all the physicians have agreed upon those, and they do not disagree in the judgment with cautery in those.
And know, children, that of the secret of healing by cautery with fire and of the goodness of it, is that fire is simple, the action of which does not reach beyond the member which is cauterized and not to the other member with it attached except with slight inconvenience.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that in the members which are far from it, and strongly makes it come in the member illness of difficult healing and strongly its use.
But fire, by its sublimity and of its substance goodness, does not do that except that it superfluously escapes, and already it is to us known by experiment and by length of service of study with the art upon the truth of the causes; and for that I am excused of the length of the sermon and if it were not that it is not written in my book in this pause to you secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and of its expulsion by which expels the illnesses, with a philosophical sermon demonstrative, the which would be acute in your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree of the time in which it is convenient to make cautery and pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient in all times, because that the inconvenience by the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which with the cautery is thrown, and more so if the cautery is for pains or of necessary pains, strong and fistulous, which do not suffer tardiness because it is feared of those that come malice, which is greater than slight inconvenience entering by time.
And thus do not catch in your minds, o, children, that this is not esteemed but by the vulgar people and the foolish physicians, because it is that to that illness which is healed by cautery is not reduced all times, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not thus as they think of that, because cautery is nothing but in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humidities which are cause for that pains come.
But however, cautery superfluously over medicine by the desire of its value and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its illness returns at any hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of its illness, and the virtue of it, and that which is prepared in the body of it of the addition of the superfluities in it, and that which is reached to it in its acquisition in foods and things similar to those causes; unless that the illness in which cautery is administered be illness subtle in member of few superfluities and humidities, as cautery of tooth for pain and things similar to that, it is possible that in it it does not return that pain, but that it is made in smalls.
And most commonly it is said that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is said rightly, for I do not understand it in this, because I believe that it is not a cure that profits by medicine nor by any other cause except cautery.
And the cause is contrary to this; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when they administer the ways of cure in some diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and then at the end of the cause one administers cautery, and it profits to that. And therefore, that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, it is not according to the understanding which the common people and most of the foolish physicians understand.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not make a scar, as it is not absolutely true, because I have already seen it and have found that it does not do so except in some bodies where others do not, and cautery with that is good and better than with iron as they said; however, when you make cautery with fire of gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want by the heat of the gold, and that it prepares to receive heat; and if you adjust it over the fire, the gold melts by the fire, and in the fire some plates so that the artisan catches by the occupation of that.
And for this reason, cautery with iron must be done more lightly and more carefully to the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head among the feet, so that afterward the one asking for it knows what he wants from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers on the humidity and coldness over the nerve accident of which there are two causes, so it is the cause of soda and multitude of rheumatic fluxes, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the ears and of the ears flowing, and multitude of sleep, and of toothache and of the goiter, and universally of all disease that comes from coldness, as well as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and similar in those diseases.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first you command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine the head modifying, for three or for four nights, according to that exHiggins the virtue of the patient and the age of him and his custom.
And then command him to shave his head, and then make that seizure between your hands on a fallen bench and that he place his hands on his feet.
And then place the razor of your palm near the nose between his heels. But however, as your saying of the middle place has been reached, sign that place with a tenta, and then ignite the cautery olive of which this is the form:
And then place that upon the place signed with a tenta, in the manner that it descends, with which your hand be constricted little by little, and you revolve that.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see already of the bone being discovered some quantity of the head, as well as the quantity of grain of errs, then raise your hand, and if not return your hand with that iron, with another of that, if it is cooled, until it is seen of the bone that I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve that over the place and leave that for three days.
And then place on it a poultice enclosed in border and leave that on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with tetrafarmacon ointment until it is healed.
And already they said that when the plague remains open, so much better gets the scar, because it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that it should be cauterized the bone inside the bone, and that the cautery should be kept until some part of the surface of the bone is burned.
And then scrape that which is burned of the bone, and then it should be cured.
And others said that with the cautery it should reach the end, until it presses into the bone forcefully until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati small: And they estimate that from that place expire the vapors of the head.
And it should be kept open for a long time, and then it should be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two kinds of cautery have not been seen at all, except in some men according to a way of fear; and leave that, of me, it is better for health, when it is; because the head is revealed by the solution of continuity of it as well as we have testified in the other members, and more so when the head of the patient is of a cold nature.
And the species of cautery first is more safe and better of me; and of that one I use and with that work with health.
Second Chapter.
Of the cautery of the head.
When throughout the head occurs chronic and long pain and this is prolonged in the patient, and uses of herbs and ointments and capipures and plasters and guats and cadels and gualinas and semblantz, and mostly if already it has been cauterized with a cautery which is recounted and does not benefit him any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of a strong creation in its nature; and is not frail and finds a great burning, then that cauterizes with another cautery besides that one a little. And then cauterizes that one on the horn of his head with a cautery until the coda is parted. Incise the coda and make it uncovered of the bone the quantity which we have recounted and cauterizes that one with a cautery in the rear part of the head in the place which is called vas, — and is that place in which is placed a cupping glass. And alleviate your hand in this, and do not uncover the bone, for the patient by this finds much great pain different from the pain of all the other cauteries of the head.
And I say this cautery in its place, because whoever cauterizes with the cautery with which the horns of the head and the occiput are cauterized is more subtle cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
Of cauterization of old-not-new migraine.
When in the part of the head pain is felt suddenly, or is stretched pain within the eye, be evacuated with medicines the head modifying, and be administered the other cure, which I have said in the divisions of the diseases; and all does not benefit, then cauterization in it is in two ways: or cauterization with acute medicine burning, or with iron.
But cauterizing with burning medicine is that you take a piece of alh, and scour that one and cut off the extremities of it from both the heads. And then incise the place of the pain in the temple with a lancet wide until there is made a place left the bone, until it is hidden.
And then strengthen over it with a stopped by descent constriction, and leave that for the spaces of three hours; and then untie the and take out the alh, and leave the plague for two or three days, and then place over it a cloth submerged in boder until the place makes a scab.
And then cure that with an enguent until it is healed.
And if you want, do this with some burning medicines which I have written in the two treatises of burning medicines.
But the cauterization with iron according to this manner:  ignite with a cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called claus clavilhs, because the head of it is as if in the form of a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small eminence.
And then place over the place of the pain, and hold your hand — so that the artery which is left is not burned — and revolve the iron little by little with velocity.
And if the quantity of it that is burned by the thickness of the bone as much as the majority of it, and elevate your hand so that the artery is not burned which is left, so that no flux of blood comes.
And then imbibe cloth in salt water and place that over the place, and leave that for three days; and then place cloth crushed with boder, and then cure with an enguent until it is healed.
And if you want, cauterize with the extremity of the knife according to cautery, and guard yourself from incision of artery in this migraine properly old-not-new.

Chapter VI.
Of cauterization of tumors.
The tumor which is cured and with cauterization is nothing but of the kinds which come from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of the diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the kind that comes from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that kind of tumor with leeches and purgatives and gargles, and if you do not feel comfort in your cure, then you must cauterize the tumor with three cauteries: the first you must at the root of the ear, the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite side of the diseased part, because softening does not come except in the part that is healing.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize that with the cautery in the right of the extremity of the ear, as sovereign a little above the corner of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which be according to the length of the finger, and pause your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the majority of the species of the cord is burned.

And then cure the place with what is oppositely shown until it is healed.

Chapter XVII.
Of cauterization of fistula that is in the lacrimal of the heel.
When you cure a fistula with that which we have said in the divisions of the ailments and do not confer your cure, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to place his head in your lap, and hold the head of him some minister between your hands in such a manner that it not be disturbed nor agitated with his head.
And then place a cloth infused in oil or in a poultice of ptilli on the heel of him.

Chapter XXI.
Of cauterizing tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to cold, or a worm is in it, or it does not respond to treatment with medicine, then cauterization is done in that tooth in two ways: cauterization with a cow's horn, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with horn is that you take the horn of a cow and heat it in a blacksmith's forge, and then take a piece of cloth and wrap it around the tip of the tentacle, and then dip that in the heated horn, and place it on the painful tooth firmly,  until it is seared.
And then repeat this several times until the power of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, dip wool or cloth in the heated horn above, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a red-hot iron on top of it until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But however, cauterization with fire is that you attend to the handle of the iron or of the fire, and that there is some thickness in its center and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cautery, the shape of which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it until the cautery is seared; and do this several times because the pain will be subdued either on that day or the next day.
And cover that after the cauterization the patient rinses his mouth with good water and keeps it there for an hour, then spits it out; and this is the shape of the cautery.

Chapter .xliv.

When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
And therefore, as gout caused by cold is cured with a method of cure and the pains are not removed, then the pains are removed with cautery.
And it is that you cauterize that after evacuation in the circuit of the joint of the foot with many cauteries.
And let it be an olive cautery of which this is the form of it:
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pains rise into the tendons or to the other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize that on each tendon with three or four cauteries of the entire part with this olive cautery.
And if many cauteries that these cauteries are necessary to you, then cauterize that and do not press too hard your hand with the cautery before, be only around the outline of the bone.
And if the pains rise into the tendon of the lower back, then administer the cautery which we have said in its chapter.
And if the pains are in the muscles only, and it is called sciatica, then prick in the circuit of the fossae thus as it revolves, prick in those two lines.
And if the pains remain in the fingers, then prick in the circuit of the fossae on each node and on the palm of the hand.
And if the pains rise to certain joints in the shoulders or to the muscles, then cauterize the certain parts of the joints.
And do not evacuate the patient of good regimen and reception of medicines, because if it is done good regimen and the evacuation is done with this cautery, it will be healed, God help.
Chapter .xlv.
Of cauterization of ruptures.
When a rupture happens in the groin and the intestines are protruding in front of the hernia, and this begins to protrude, then it is necessary that you order the patient to leave their food for the day and that they use lenient causes so that the wound descends from their belly.
And then hold the patient between your hands over their back, and command him to keep his leg straight until the hernia is thrown or the intestines appear.
And then return that with your hands and feel with your fingers the rupture over the bones of the pelvis with a sign the extremity of which is similar to the majority of a circle in the upper parts of the body.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form of it:
until it be very hot and throws sparks. And then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area so that the intestine does not come out.
You have already opened the space between the patient's thighs, placed a cushion under them, another servant on their legs, and another on their chest, holding their hands.
And then place the cautery on that sign with your hand with the cautery standing straight, and hold that until with it you can feel the bones of the pelvis into the middle of the groin; and repeat with that another time if with that you have not succeeded in the first attempt into the bone.
And observe carefully the position of the intestine during the cauterization, so that you do not burn the intestine so that it does not come to death or other great harm to the patient.
And know that when you have the cautery do not touch the bone, do not compromise your operation.
And know that the cautery of children should be subtle according to their size and measure.
And after carefully care for the cauterized area for three days until the scar of the fire is healed.
And after care for that with the other ointments until it is healed.
And the patient should lie on their back for forty days until the area and the plague are sealed.
And know that you should pause the nourishment of him according to the length of time of his cure, which the lines his belly, and that the intestine should not come out due to the effort of healing.
And after, when he wants to stand up, after forty days, then administer him decent food, and keep that for another forty days.
And be moderate in work and in the repletion of food and drink, and of voice vehemently, for when he uses this regimen of healing entirely he will be healed.
And you should say the cure of ruptures in the other parts of the belly, and so at the beginning, and you want them not to pull, then cauterize the rupture of that with a round cautery according to the quantity of it, and it is that which is extracted from the codena as if it were the third part of it; and after care for that with what we have said, and it is not adjusted.
And already some first ones say that rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery according to this form, because it is marked with a tenta:
And it is placed a line that goes by the latitude in the broadest part of the rupture, and another line below; and place your hand with a pointed cautery, but the first cautery is lighter and better.
Chapter .xlvi.
Of cauterization of torsion.
When in some members by accident or by percussion pain and that pain persists for a long time and does not help in the cure with medicines, then know that you should cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And be the cautery of every member according to its magnitude and its smallness, and its virtue and weakness, and location of torsion and pain of it.
Therefore, if it is healed by the first cautery, well is; and if not, then repeat over it the cautery; for by custom of those pains it is that they are pointed of member to that member which approaches to it, so that know that you should cauterize those until the patient is healed.
Chapter .xlvii.
Of cauterization of leprosy.
Leprosy some times is cauterized by great benefit, and especially if it is the kind of leprosy that is made by putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
And therefore, as you want to cauterize that, consider if the leprosy is common and has that cured with what we have said in the division and do not desist, nor is it, and fear over the patient that the corruption comprehends the whole body of it and the whole complexion of it, then cauterize that over the head with 5 cauteries: one in the middle of the head, and the second further down from it, and the front to the end of the hair; and two on two horns; and one behind, on the nape or service.
And finish your hand with the cautery a little while before it imprints on the bone a small impression, and from it the scabs be displaced, so that the expiration of thick vapors be alleviated from it; and cauterize over the flesh according to what is necessary.
And if the leprosy is already expanded over the patient and appears manifestly, then know that you should cauterize that with those cauteries the ones which we have said in the head; and with a cautery over the extremity of the nose, and with two cauteries over the two cheekbones, and with two cauteries over two vertebrae of the neck, and with six cauteries over the vertebrae of the back, and one large one over the vertebrae near the hip, and one over the ribs, and with two over the knees, and one over each knee, and with two over the elbows, and with two over the muscles, and with two over the tendons of their feet; and cauterize that over all the joints of the fingers of the hands and the feet, and over each heel of their feet, and over the hollows of their arms.
And guard yourself from the nerves which are on the heel that you do not burn those.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery over the bone of the palate and with another over the mouth of the stomach, and another over the liver.
And know that as much as you adjust cauteries, so much is it more beneficial and more conferent; and know that the patient does not have in the cautery pain, as if they have their own, because for that the body of it is already stupefied.
And know that the cauteries should be great or few according to the members and the joints according to what is preceded by the species of the tools.
And then carefully apply the cautery to the surface with a mixture of flour, honey, and the other remedy while it is healing.
Chapter XLVIII.
Of the cauterization of stupor.
When any limb is numbed or asleep and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then you cauterize that numbed limb with a cautery according to what merits the size of the limb or its smallness.
And let your cautery enter the depth of the bone a little. And then carefully apply that with an ointment while it is healing.
And sometimes, certain stupors are cauterized which extend to the arms and legs, and to the vertebrae of the lower back and the spaces of the nerves which supply that limb, and the stupor is removed.
But do not presume to do this except for one who is wise in the anatomy of the limbs and the egress of the nerves throughout the entire body.
Chapter XLIX.
Of the cauterization of ulcers that are mortified.
When an ulcer is old and does not respond to any of the medicinal ointments, then you cauterize over it with a cautery, pricking it a little, according to the quantity of the depth of the bone, until the whiteness and color of it are removed, and the color of it is changed.
And then carefully apply that with a mixture of flour, lentils, and rose oil, and with arnica leaves, and either pigeon's blood or round robin's blood, from each one a part, and all mixed together, and then apply a linen cloth and place it on the spot until it is healed.
Chapter L.
Of the cauterization of crabs.
When a cancer begins and you want to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference as it is turned.
And some wise men say that it should be cauterized with the pointed cautery in the middle place; but to me this is not seen, because I fear that it will be ulcerated, and I have already seen this some times.
And it is more proper that it be cauterized around its circumference with a circular cautery as we have said, or with a moving cautery.
Chapter LI.
Of the cauterization of abscesses.
When some abscess is delayed in maturation, and this is because of the superfluity that causes it, or because of the patient's age, who is old or decrepit, with little blood, or because of time, and you want to hasten the maturation of the abscess; then cauterize around it with a small, moving cautery, and then leave it so that it will hasten in maturation.
But if you want the perforation of it with a cautery, then you ignite the cautery, the shape of which is this: and pause that in the middle place of the abscess until it penetrates the bone.
And if the cautery in that place that is furthest, so that the body of the arm be relieved; and then carefully apply that until it is healed.
Chapter LII.
Of the cauterization of corrodents.
A corrodent is a corruption that walks in the limb, which corrodes it as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see that corrodent in a place that suffers cauterization with fire, then you ignite small, moving cauteries, and large ones according to what is convenient in that place where the corrodent is.
And then cauterize that from all sides until you eradicate all the corrosion and no cause of it remains.
And then leave it for three days, and place over the cauterized places a compress with oil mixed until all the scars are eradicated and all the corruption is gone.
And then carefully apply that with ointments that generate flesh.
But if after three days you see that the flesh grows healthy in which there is no corruption, it is good; but if not, then repeat the cauterization over what is raw in the corrupted places.
And a corrodent is medicated some times with sharp medicine, which that is placed in the place of cautery. But nevertheless, cauterization with fire is of more gentle help.
And I have already said the cure of it with sharp medicine in the division, and therefore take that when you have need of it.
Chapter LIII.
Of the cauterization of warts and other similar things.
Many times there is a malady on the lower parts of the foot called a wart, and it is a rough, protruding cause, which makes the foot lame; and cauterization in those is done in two ways, so it is cauterization with fire and cauterization with boiling water.
But cauterization with fire is that you ignite the cautery concave in the shape of a vulture's beak, which is made of iron according to the quantity which contains the wart from all sides, and is of subtle margins.
And then place that ignited one over the wart, and then revolve your hand with the cautery around the circumference of the wart until the cautery reaches the depth of the wart. And let him rest for three days before he begins to throw up. And apply a poultice made with wild herbs crushed with salt to that, and leave the poultice on it for a night, so that it is eradicated from its roots.
And treat the area with a gargle of generative meat until it is healed.
And if it is not converted, and many times it happens on the surface of the body, mostly in the hands and feet, then you must administer cauterization to those with water, and take a small quantity of lead or iron or vulture's bone, and place it on the boil; and then pour a little water into the cavity of the tool, and hold your hand, and you revolve that with the pressure of your hand, and press the edge of the tool into the root of the boil, and it will draw the water into the root of the boil; and wait for the patient a little while for the bite of the water for an hour, and then remove it, because the boil with its roots will be eradicated.
And so do this to those and the other until you come upon all of them on their body.
And treat those pus that the roots of the boils are eradicated with this water that the flesh generates.
Chapter .liiii.
Of cauterization of tremor.
When someone has a tremor due to heat in the nerve or fever of heat, or for some similar cause, then you must cauterize that with four cauteries or five on the vertebrae of the back, between each vertebra with a cautery; and with a cautery on the feet of him, and on his stomach, with an olive cautery.
And the tremor of him will be rested and hastened the health of the feverish illness.
Chapter .lv.
Of cauterization of white spots accidents on the body.
When on the body are spots white, and are pustules split that are made of thick corrupted matter; therefore at the beginning when it appears, that it be cauterized over the top of the fistula with a subtle cautery with twigs of myrtle, the extremity of which is extended with fire; or with roots of erestologia long; or with a lenticular cautery.
And sometimes it is cauterized additionally at the beginning of its expulsion in this manner; and if they are not believed, and the superfluity is ruptured, then those, and it heals from those.
But however, it must be done after evacuation with phlebotomy.
Chapter lvi.
Of cauterization of flux of blood accident by incision of artery.
Many times there is a flux of artery that is incised, the plague which must be forced, or due to the incision of abscesses or cauterization of the member, and then similar, and it is difficult to remove that.
Therefore, when it happens to someone, then you must tightly grasp with your hand the orifice of the artery, and place over it your finger, stretching that many times until it stops the flux of blood from your finger, and that it does not come out.
And place in the fire the olive cauteries few and large, by number many, and exhale over them while they are burning.
And take from those one small or one large according to the place and the plague in which the artery is ruptured, over that vein, quickly, as you have removed your finger, and bring the cautery until it is abcised and constricted that blood.
And if the blood is expelled from the orifice of the artery when you remove your finger and extract the cautery, then take another cautery tightly from the cauteries that in the fire are prepared, and therefore do not cease to do this one after another until the blood is constricted.
And guard yourself that you do not burn the nerve that is here, and that it comes upon the patient another malice.
And know that when from the artery flows blood, then it is not possible in those to constrict the blood, and especially when the artery is large, if not by one of four ways: or with cautery as we have said, or with extraction when it is not extracted, because when it is extracted the extremities of him are burned well and the blood is constricted, or that it be tied with a thread or with a ligament for strong structure, or that they be placed upon him medicines of which the virtue is to restrict the blood; and be tightened with a cushion with decent constriction.
But he who administers decent constriction of him with a ligament and with structure with cloths or by position of burning causes and similar, do not confer otherwise than briefly.
But if this happens to someone and the physician is not present nor medicine, then open with the placement of the finger indicated over the orifice of that vein as we have said, and understand to the great constriction of it until the blood is stopped from the sovereign part of the plague, and over the artery the finger is not removed; and over the artery be sprinkled with cold water of much great coldness until the blood is congealed and thickened; and more cossire in which he has to cauterize or of medicine necessity.

Chapter Second.

Chapter V.
Of the cure of lagremas by catartz and in the heels descending from the parts of the inside of the head.

Chapter VI.
Of the cure of that which catz in the ears.
Every cause that catz in the ears is one of four species, either it is a mineral stone or a similar cause to stone, such as iron and lead, or it is of a plant, such as celery or beans, or it is a fluid cause, such as water and sour wine and their likenesses, or some beast.
And therefore when stone catz in the ear or another cause similar to those causes that do not fit or grow in the ear, and puts the ear in the sun, and if you see the stone, then distill in it some cause of violet oil or sesame, and then administer the extract of it, and make the patient to snort with a condition, and plug their nostrils to prevent the occurrence of snorting. And then put in the circuit of the ear some pieces of cloth or wool, and extend the ear to the parts above, because many times it is thrown out with these causes.
And if it is not thrown out, then administer the extract of it with the instrument called a gesti epicicarios subtle, of which this is the form:
And if it is thrown out with the gesti, well is; and if not, then administer the extract of it with a subtle onci of little duplication.
And therefore if it is not thrown out by this, then make a canula of brass and introduce the extremity of the canula into the tract of the ear and close around the canula with wax and softened oil so that it be not open except the canula. And then extract with your wind with a strong attraction, as many times as with the water that we have recounted.
But if it is not thrown out in this manner, then take some halka lit or of a vetch apparelled with which the birds are taken a small quantity, and put that in the extremity of a ray, and then envelop over that well-placed cot. And then cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of the descending water of the wound.
We have already said the species of water in the division and which one it is convenient to perforate with a serum, declaring, then this according to the health.
Then, you must make the patient lie between your hands on a cushion and tie his wound tightly.
And then place your left hand near the eyelid of his wound if the wound in which is the water is the left; or on your right hand, if the wound is the right.
And then with your right hand take the almond, if the wound is left; or with your left hand, if the wound is right.
And then place the tip of the almond near the crown for the thickness of the ray in the album of the wound from the side of the lacrimal gland, and then press the almond with virtue and roll your hand on it.
And then penetrate into the album of the wound and feel that the almond has already arrived at the void cause.
And it is necessary that the measure of the path of the almond to the tip be the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness, and it is the crown of the wound; because you will see with that pupil the vision of the wound through the clarity of the cornea.
And then place the almond into the place where is the water, and then you throw it down once, then another, and therefore if the water descends so quickly, then wet the patient's wound with water over which he has his sight immediately, and almond in his wound.
And then rest for a while; therefore if the water has descended, then you put that other one back down as long as the almond is not thrown.
And therefore when it is dried and does not descend, then you extract the almond with ease, and roll it with your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a little clear salt of gemma and with that wash the wound carefully; and then place outside the wound cotton or stopper or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white and lick the wound with water.
But not in those who are of our time, place on that comi trissat with egg white.
And if you do not obey your almond to the entrance of the wound due to its hardness — because it is some of the men whose wound is very hard — then it is necessary that you take the spatula which is called alberid of which this is the shape:
And therefore pierce with that that conjuncture, and do not end your hand in the track, and it is not if you do not make a way for the almond to the subtle place.
And then introduce the almond according to what we have said.
And you must complete the work, prepare the patient for sleep in a quiet, dark room where they lie on their back, and forbid all movement.
And keep him in nature so that his nature is purified, and do not turn his head to the right or left at all.
And bind him according to his disposition on the third day.
And then unbind him in that dark room and prohibit the cold air, and make him see some causes, and then return the binding on the seventh day.
And do not let him do this at the hour of cures or soon after the infusion. You must have him do this so that the water flows lightly through the great and vehement of regard.
But if an abscess occurs, then you must unbind the wound before the seventh day, and rectify it with water that comes from the abscess.
Then you close the eyes of him and place your hand on the face of him through which the movement of him is regulated, leaving him for several days, him existing in the dark room.
And then he is taken out of that room gradually and converses about his causes.
And know that in alchemy, the disciple of vision is not excused some times, and then you shall be bold about the operation.
And we have arrived at some of those who are in the Artach, and some say that they make fire in the Ayrac magdaam perforated with which water is sucked.
But however, I have not seen in our land anyone who had perfect water, nor is water mentioned in some of the books of the ancients; and it is possible that this is new.
And these are the forms of the species of magdaan so that it is above those who ignore those:
And they are made of copper or iron properly, and their extremities are with this triangular subtlety, the acute extremity as such is the form.
Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of flesh nothing in the nose.
When in the nose are born diverse flesh growths of which some cause is assembled like a scorpion of moth weight, or a polyp weight; and this ailment is called polyp because of the resemblance to that weight represented. And of it is cancerous flesh, lapped, of brown color; and of it is that flesh lion not of brown color.
Therefore in that which is in these lion flesh not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must have the patient be seated between your hands and placed in the sun, and hue the nostrils of him, and pick your onci in those flesh. And then extract that to the outer parts, and then incise the water that you have comprehended of those with a sharp, subtle spatula from one part until you know that all the flesh is gone; if any cause of it remains, of which the abscision is possible, then you root that water with one of the subtle instruments with ease until nothing of it remains. But if it bleeds or an abscess occurs, then you pause to him what you must; or if it is of the malignant abscesses, then you cauterize it until it is abscindit blood and all the cavities are gone.
And then be placed in the nose after the incision vi agre and water or wine. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds humidity into the palate, then you know that it is already healed.
But if the humidity does not penetrate as you must, then you know that from it is flesh nothing in the pus sobiras bones of the nose to which the abscision has not reached.
Therefore then you must introduce a thread of it into which there is some thickness, and use in it moth nuts, and place between each nut the quantity of the finger or less, and engage the patient and introduce one extremity of the thread into the nose with the ray or with another cause which is to it possible.
And as that will have done, that it will throw its odor into the canals of the nose, and be spit on the throat, because troops of times the semblance to this action do the children at the schools, and is lighter cause to him who wants to do it.
And then place the two extremities of the thread, one extremity that goes out over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a lock of flesh with the nuts that are in the thread, and do this until you know that the flesh is already with the nuts of the thread.
And then extract the thread, and place in the nose after the abstraction of the blood a poultice, and do this for three days or more until the ointment corrodes all that is remaining of the flesh.
And at the end of the cause, place in the nose a lead pipe for several days until it is healed.
But if you are in need of a cure that requires, use of that.
And this is the form of the instrument to capipurge maker with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nose:
And make it of silver or copper, which is similar to a small open lamp, as such as a small conch, and the meat similarly.
And if you wish, make a closed canula like a tube, and the tube of the instrument to be used for purging should be flat, uncovered; to which have a handle at the back of it, with which you hold it when you heat oil or water in it that you wish from the suckable causes.
Chapter XXV.
Of the nails in the extremities of the nose.
Many times the nail in the extremities of the nose is seen, and it is magnified and mentioned in some days within which it is not seen.
And for that, you must insist on that at the beginning of its appearance, and eradicate all of it. And then place on the area a cautery or medicine that is burning, the one which is in place of it.
But if its incision is delayed until it is magnified, then consider if it is calcified, hard, of dark color and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron, for it is a dangerous abscess; for many times that one who incides this abscess, should suffer great malice from the one who had it.
And if the abscess is of a light touch and not of dark color, and sometimes that incision is possible in all of it, then evacuate the patient and incisions that without fear, and cure the area with water that is required and constrict within which it is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of suturing the nose and the lips and the ear when continuity is dissolved by plague or by similarities.
Know that when accidents happen dissolution of continuity in one of these cartilages, little confidence is given in that operation unless in some men.
Therefore, when it is necessary to have some cause of those, that you consider if it is fresh plague with its blood, and then you adjust the two lips of the plague with suture, and then cure that until it is healed.
And if the lips of dissolution of continuity are already separated, and each is made healthy, then it is necessary that you excoriate each part of its apparent tendon until blood comes out. And then adjust the two lips with suture and strengthen those, and over those pulverize blood of dragon and incense, and place over the powder a piece of diaphana plaster, or of some other of the consolidating plasters, and leave that tied for two days or three, and then untie that and change that plaster and leave that until the filaments are by themselves separated, and then cure with an enguent until it is healed.
But the manner of the suture is that you add the dissolution of continuity or with needles as we have recommended in the suture of the belly, or add the dissolution of continuity with thread as you have been taught.
Chapter XXVII.

Chapter XXVIII.
Of incision of the flesh adjusted in the gums.
Greatly often there are on the gums flesh adjusted the which the ancients called albulus, therefore it is necessary that you suspend that with tongs or that you have that with the forceps and incision that you must cut its root, and let the blood run or the blood.

Chapter XXIX.
Of the reason of teeth with iron.

Chapter .xxx.
Of the Eradication of Teeth.
Take care that you cure the tooth of its pain with all skill and take your time in the entire eradication of it, for there is no cause that should supplant the vigor of it when it is eradicated, for it is substance sublimated within that the excuse in the eradication of it.
But take care when the patient is forced to have that tooth eradicated, that you firmly must certify which is the aching tooth, for many times the pain deceives the patient and makes it seem as though it is in a healthy tooth, and you eradicate that one and then the pain does not cease until the bad and aching tooth is eradicated, for we have already seen this by the operation of the barbers.
Therefore, as you must be certified which is the aching tooth, and that you know well, then you must scarify in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth of the gums of all parts, and then you must pull that out with your fingers, or with subtle forceps at the beginning little by little until that you conquer it.
And then, in order to have a good hold, use strong pincers or a strong hold, and place the head of the patient between your teeth that you have well, so that it does not harm, and then pull the tooth according to straightness in a manner that you do not break it, nor give the patient greater pain.
And therefore, if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments, and put that one to the tooth from all parts with facility and exert the removal of it in such a way that it is done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then you must take a piece of cloth and wrap that around the broken part with the extremity of a fine ray so that it is not broken in the hour of your constriction upon it with the pliers.
And you must work skillfully with scarification in the circuit of all parts of the gums and guard well your strength that you do not break it and remain a part of it, and return upon the patient for the malice that it is greater than the first pain of it.
And guard yourself that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their fisting and audacity over the eradication of them, since they do not administer what we have recommended; for many times they make come upon the men ailments great ones which are more difficult to be broken, and the roots of them remaugulated all, or some of those, or that you extract that with some bones of the jaw as in many times we have testified.
And after the eradication of it, the mouth should be washed with wine caut or wine agre with salt.
And if it should flow blood for this, as many times it should, then sprinkle some quantity of zegi and asperge it upon the wound, and if you do not confer that zegi, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and the subtle pliers with which the tooth is pulled at the beginning should be of long extremity, of short handle and thick, so that they are not bent when you must work with them.
And they should be as times of thick handle so that when you tighten them with those they are not bent, they should be short extremities.
And they should be made of Indian iron, carefully made of straight extremities, and in the extremities of those there should be teeth of which some interlock in others and tighten by strong constriction, and sometimes the extremities of those are the shape of the beak of a bird which has the name ciconia, so it is called a "spoon", and they are of strong constriction.
Chapter .xxxi.

Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of the prominent teeth above the others.
When the teeth are prominent not according to their natural course, for those the form is lacking, and mostly when it happens to women, and mostly to the venerable old ones; therefore, since you consider: if a tooth is nothing near another tooth, and it is not possible to suture or liniment it, then root that; but that it is not attached to another tooth, then you incise it with this instrument of which this is the shape; and it is similar to a pig's snout, and it is made of Indian iron of a sharp moving extremity.
And be your incision with which you incise it in several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and that it is not damaged by other teeth.
And if the prominent tooth is exposed to filing, then file that with a file of Indian iron of which this is the shape:
And be all of Indian iron the margin and very well; and be of small moving points as a file with which needles are made, with which the tooth be filed little by little in several days with facility, so that no other tooth be damaged and broken. And then line that at the end, and seize that with some razors.
And if the tooth of which one part is twisted and licks the tongue, then when you file it until the projection of that fraction is stayed and smoothed, and be filled so that the tongue does not lick it nor the word is broken.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the restoration of damaged teeth with gold or silver wire.
When accidents happen to the teeth in front with concussion and removal by percussion or by fall, and the patient cannot strengthen over that which he manages, and you have cured it with styptic medicines, and it has not been of any use your cure, then because it does not break, it is made in those that are strengthened with gold wire and not with silver, because silver becomes green and soon, but gold never changes.
And be the wire in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that it can enter between the teeth; and the shape of the straight is that you take the wire and take double of it between two healthy teeth, and then that you curve it with two tortuosities of the wire between two damaged ones, or if it is one or several, until it reaches the healthy tooth of the other part. And then iterate the tightening into the part of which you began, and strengthen your hand with facility and wisdom so that it is not damaged.
And be your tightening with which you strengthen the wire the roots of the teeth so that it does not escape.
And then incise the superfluous extremities of the wire with the forceps or tweezers, and add those in each place with gesture, and convert those and hide them between the healthy tooth and the damaged one, so that it does not cause injury to the tongue. And then leave it that tight like a Roman.
But if it is loosened or broken, strengthen it or those with another wire in such a manner in all its time.
And this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the straightening of two healthy teeth and two damaged ones, as well as sometimes these are tied:
And when it is done that a tooth or two are returned to their places after the fall of each one, and they are recut as we have recounted, and that they are damaged.
And this is done only by a good artificer and wise.
And sometimes it is adapted some cause of the bones of the cow, and it is made as such as the shape of a tooth, and it is placed in the place where the tooth is missing, and it is strengthened as we have said, and remains and serves with that for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the incision of the ligament which comes in the tongue and prohibits speech.
This ligament which comes from the tongue some times or is natural with which man is born, or accidental and happens by plague which is already consolidated.
And the operation in it is that men open the mouth of the patient, his head existing in the tieu se; and elevate his tongue, and then incise that ligament nerve according to the latitude so that the tongue is loosened from its recess.
But if in that there is some hardness or knotting, and this is due to the consolidation of plague, then you throw a point and cut it along the latitude as long as you have incised the ligament and the knotting is dissolved.
And guard yourself that no fissure is made in the skin of the flesh and that you cut here the artery and blood comes.
And then wash the traces of the incision with water or with wine or with cold water; and then place under the tongue; so is the method which holds the patient of the tongue in any night so that it is not consolidated another time.
But if blood flows, place on the location vitriol crushed; but if the blood comes, then cauterize the location with a cauterizing iron which convenes to this. And then this cure with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the extraction of a ranula from the tongue.
Sometimes an abscess happens on the tongue resembling a small lump which prohibits the tongue from its natural operation; and often it is magnified as long as the mouth is open.
And the operation in it is that men open the mouth of the patient seeing in front of the sun and considers the abscess.
And if you see it of a dark color or of a black, hard, which the patient does not feel, then do not touch that because it is a cancer.
And if it is inclined to white, in which there is humidity, then you put the point in it, and incise it with a subtle spatula, and incise it from all parts; and if blood comes to you in the hour of your operation, then you place crushed vitriol above it, so that it is restrained the blood.
And then return to your work until you had treated it with compliment of it, until it is washed with wine and salt; and cure this with the other cure to water until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxvi.
Of the extraction of abscesses of the ears and of that which is nothing in the throat and of the other abscesses.
When in the throat there is a swelling, so are the glands which are assembled swollen, which happen outwards and are called abscesses of the ears, which when you cure them with water as we have said in the division and it is not healed, then consider if the abscess is hard, of a dark color, of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of a red color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron because of the flow of blood; abandon it until it is ripe, and then either you will draw it out, or it will burst by itself.
And if it is of a white color, soft, and the root of it is subtle, then that is to be incised.
And the operation in it is that you consider, before your operation, if the abscess of it has already rested with a complete rest or if it has diminished with some diminution; and then do so that the patient stands in front of the sun, and his head be in the tieu se, and open the mouth of him, and the servant takes between his hands presses the tongue of him with an instrument noble of which this is the form:
And it is made of silver or of brass, and it is subtle like a knife.
Therefore, as you press with that the tongue and it is shown to you the abscess, and catz upon that the tieu vezement, then take a point and place it in the amenla, and pull that to the parts outwards as much as you can. Other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then incise that with the instrument of which this is the form:
Other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then incise that with the instrument of which this is the form: And it is assembled to forceps, but the extremities of it are curved, so that the orifice of each one is in the right of the other, very sharp, which is of iron indi embedded.
But if this instrument is not present to you, then incise that with a spatula of which this is the form of it: And it is sharp on one part, not sharp on the other part.
And since you have incised a groove, incise the other according to this same manner of incision, and then the incision the patient guards with cold water
But if there is a flow of blood, guard with water of decoction of the bark of millefolium or of myrtle leaf and similar to that of the stiptic causes until the flow of blood is restrained, and then cure this until it is healed.
And sometimes there are born in the throat other abscesses other than those of the ears, and incise those according to what I have said in the incision of two grooves equally.
And I have already treated a woman of an abscess which was in the throat of her, which abscess tended to a brownish color, of little feeling, which had already closed the throat of her, and the woman breathed with tight meat, and had already prohibited her from eating and drinking water, and had already arrived at death if may have lasted for a day or two.
And the abscess had already grown so much that it had two openings through which it exited.
Therefore, I treated her fisturally and placed myself in one of the openings, and pulled out that one, and it was thrown from her a large portion, and then I incised that one from where it understood from the other opening, and then I opened the mouth of it, and I compressed her tongue, and then I placed the opening in that abscess.
And then I abscised a large portion of it, and it was not flowing from it except a little blood. Therefore, the throat of that woman was absolutely clear, and she began to drink water, and then she ate food, therefore I did not cease to incise that abscess many times for a long time, and a succession of abscesses succeeded in place of that one, which incision extended while that one was prolonged.
Therefore, I brought a needle and cauterized the throat of her, therefore as much as an addition; and then I walked around and did not know what God had done to her after that.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of incision of a boil when it is an abscess.
When catarr rises in the boil, and it is an abscess and it is long, then it is called perpendicular; and if it is in the part below thick and round, and then it is called a bubo.

And if you want, take a cotton and envelopes that over the extremity of the ray, and immerse the cotton in the medicine, and introduce the ray with the cotton in a tube of above until the cotton adheres in that tube, and do this as many times until you achieve what you want of the cauterization of the uvula, and then leave that as it dries and falls off after about three days or four.
And if you wished to repeat the medicine, repeat that one, and after the cauterization, abstain from the circuit of the uvula with cotton dipped in border, and modify with that which is in the circuit of it of the medicine, and be washed with cold water, and be cured for the time being with embrocation, and give gargles until it is healing.

Sometimes the uvula is cured with that which is more subtle than cauterization and incision, because it is cured with subfumigation in this manner:  Receive calament, ysop, origua, ruda, scicados arabic, camomilla, broyda and similar to those of the herbs, and adjust all those causes, or some of them, in an olla, and be submerged with strong wine, and boil; and the olla be well washed with decent lut, and be in the middle of the olla a hole, on which be placed an instrument concavity of Aram according to this manner; be made of silver or Aram.
And the extremity is introduced into the mouth of the patient until the vapor reaches the uvula over the pharynx, until the uvula is moved and obscured.
And then repeat this motion several times until it is dry, and be careful not to do this treatment at the beginning of the development of abscesses, because it would too much tighten the abscess, and in the case that you do this, you must declare the abscess of him by cautery.
But if this instrument is not at your disposal, then take a cane and compose on the extremity of it a hollow of wood, so that the mouth of the patient is covered, because the hollow of the wood prohibits the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter .xxxviii.
Of the extraction of splinters and of that which adheres in the throat and of the other causes.
Many things adhered in the throat or splinter of wood or any other cause.
