And what does not appear and is to you hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because forcibly the cause annexed to the throat is thrown-up by vomit; or that the patient swallows a piece of bread or a root of lettuce or a piece of dry bread; or prepare a piece of dry sea sponge, and tie that firmly with thread, and then the patient swallows that, because when it reaches the place in which the spines are and is extracted, then it is thrown-up. And more, take an eel and bind it with thread, and its end is placed and gently extracted; or take a porcupine and gently its spines and gently the other end.
But if they are not thrown-up with those causes which we have said, then use an instrument of lead according to this form:
And it is thicker than a ray, and in the extremity of it is a concavity which you introduce into its throat with ease.
And hold its head elevated upwards, and be careful that the touch of its bone of the throat, so that it is not forced to its body and with that which it pushes the bone or the splinter, or that the physician with his hand.
But however, that the patient that is introduced is better, for his knowledge of the place of the cause annexed and pushes it down, and pulls his hand with the instrument upwards, all that according to the quantity which is prepared for him before it is thrown-up.
Chapter .xxxix.
Of the extraction of bloodsucker annexed to the throat.
When the bloodsucker is medicated with what we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not confer, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you have compresses the tongue of him with the instrument which to you have we have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the bloodsucker, extract that with a small hook or with a subtle gesture gently.
And if it is not possible to extract with that, then take a concave cannula and introduce that into the throat of the patient, and place in the concavity of the cannula a burning iron, and do this as many times (until the bloodsucker is dead and is removed from the throat) and abstain from the patient all day of water.
And then prepare a vessel full of cold water, and work the mouth of him in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow from that any cause and bad the water one hour after another with his hand, because the bloodsucker as soon as it feels the water catz.
But if it is not thrown-up with what we have recommended, then subfumigate the patient with cimet or with asafoetida by the instrument which we have recommended in the subfumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so that it falls.
And it is another way of operation in the subfumigation of that, is that you take a bowl in which are burning embers and the bowl is covered with a cover in the middle of which is a hole, and it is composed in that hole the extremity of the instrument; and then let descend the subfumigation; and place the patient his mouth in the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the subfumigation is not thrown-up until you know that the subfumigation has reached the bloodsucker, because the bloodsucker immediately falls.
And if it does not fall, then you repeat the subfumigation many times, and abstain from the patient from drinking, and eat salty and dry causes, and do not drink water, and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it is thrown-up.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, unless that in it there is some curvature: The one which is placed in the throat, and the extremity of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is blunt, in which it is sharpened with a file, so that, when compressing any cause, that does not leave it.
Chapter .xl.
In which is the sum of the speech concerning abscesses and their incision.
Abscesses are special matters, of many kinds, according to the remembrance of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in perforation and incision of them by two manners, of which one is by the kind of abscesses in themselves; and by that which we understand of the humidities.
And the second manner is according to the places where they occur in the body, for the abscess occurring in the head is another from the abscess occurring in the buttock; and the abscess in the fleshy place is another from the abscess occurring in the joint; and to each of them is its own treatment by operation.
And more than abscesses there are some which ought not to be perforated but upon the maturation of the sania in those or the completion of them.
There are other abscesses which ought to be lanced when they are ripe, and not upon the completion of them, such as abscesses that are near the joints, for when an abscess occurs near a joint, its being is prolonged until it is able to corrupt the ligaments or nerves of that joint, so that it is made a cause of contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near a principal member, and if you delay the lancing of it until it is mature, it will cause harm to the principal member; or it is near the buttock, therefore lance it before it is ripe; and do not lance it when it is crude, of incomplete digestion, but that which is near the buttock, so that you may not be able to reach the perineum of it and extend it to the parts of the buttock, and make a fistula, or that it may be done in the term of it that it may not be healed. But more, you ought to know the hour of the lancing of the abscess, and thus it is when it is ripe.
And know that it is ripe when there is the cessation of pain and the cessation of fever, and upon the diminution of the heat and of the pulse, and the acuteness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
And that you ought to know the lancing to be done in the place furthest from the abscess and from pus coming from the cure of the eminence.
And lancing always be by the length of the flesh or of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the arms or of the feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, afterwards, in all places equal in which there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use of lancing according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, then it is better to let the lancing of it until its digestion is confirmed according to the completion, as we have said; for if you lance it before that, it prolongates the course of its power and of much dirtiness, and therefore the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are lanced according to the latitude of the flesh or of the body as necessity demands, or according to what the member requires.
And you ought to administer small lancing, and in the large abscesses large lancing and wide or many incisions according to the diversity of the greatness of the abscesses.
And others are of abscesses in which the incision ought to be concave and be incised, when it is done so that bread is made and it is done in the term that it already follows, such as those that occur in heaps of boils and buboes.
And of those are those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those is the one in which it is incised as the figure of a myrtle leaf, as the abscesses of the angles.
And of those are those in which a round incision and a lunar incision, and similar to those, are administered.
But that one to whom there is no such as his abscesses are superficial, you ought to lance that with a superficial incision, or flat only.
And you ought when the abscess is large and has already collected much sania, to lance it and not be covetous that you extract all the pus in that hour; having extracted from it one part, and then close the abscess until the next day, and then extract a greater part, and so do this many times according to the gradation until it is healed.
And especially if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, for the animal spirit many times is resolved with the egress of the sania, and therefore the patient may die, and you operate on them.
And guard this chapter with great care, and in the lancing of these abscesses, you ought to abstain from plagues and consider therefore if the plague of the abscess is little, or a flat incision, then you administer the poultices of it or of cotto anti-septic; and if the abscess is large, and the incisions of the lancing are many, then you ought to put meca in each one until they arrive together.
And if in the abscess is incised a part of the incision or has concaved that in the circuit, then you ought to cover it with old cotto or a thread made of cloth of it, as when you have treated poultices or razors, its humidity; and strengthen that within the third day; and then process that and cure it with that which is ought of the ointments until it is healed.
But if blood flows during the operation, then you administer cold water and wine in which you have soaked a cloth, and place it on the location of the blood flow many times.
But if the bleeding persists, then you must administer treatment and care, and follow the powders that I have recommended in many places in this very book and of division.
But if it is in winter, and the location of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you must enclose powders in wine and hot oil, and place them on the location.
And if it is in summer, and the locations are fleshy, then you must place powders soaked in water and oil or in wine and oil, and all that be cold until the third day, as we have said, and then you must open the abscess and cleanse it and administer to its cure what is convenient to it until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of every abscess in what manner is the way of its cure by chapters individually.
Chapter .xli.
Of the incision of abscesses which come in the neck of the head.
In the neck of the head small abscesses, and they are of a kind of nodes which contain tunics that are to their making; and the kinds of them are many.
And of them are pimples, and of those it is that contain humidity similar to lime. And of those are those that contain humidity similar to dust, and resembling to them; and of those are those that are stony, hard.
And in the incision of all, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as you must the extraction of those does not make contrary artery.
And the operation in incision of those is that you probe those with an instrument the shape of which comes near thus, the one which is called entromes, as long as you know that it contains.
Because if that which contains is humidity, then you split it with a section according to the length by superficial section according to this form:
And begins in the section of the line of .B. within to the line of .G. Therefore, as the humidity is evacuated, then you excoriate that skin that contains that humidity, and do not leave of that any cause of all, because troops many times return, if there remain of that any cause.
And then you submerge a cloth in Egyptian wash, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill with that the wound and leave it in for another day, because with that you corrode all that is raw of that skin.
And then repeat on that cloth with Egyptian wash second and third time if you need it, until you are confident that there is no longer any raw cause of that skin; then cure the wound with wash until it is healed.
And if the abscess contains fatty nodes, then you incise it according to this form: with a section having the form of a cross, and get oncis between two lips of the section and scrape it from all parts, and exert your strength in the extraction of the tunic which contains that.
But if your artery makes opposition, then do what I have recounted to you first.
And similarly do in the stony abscess of incision and cure according to what I have told you; and incision on a stony abscess is easier, because it is of little blood and of little humidity.
And some times there are some of these abscesses which are in the head in some men with which there is no humidity at all; the cause of which is because I incised on an abscess in the head of an old woman and brought back the abscess as a hard, rough, white, which could not be punctured, and if anyone was struck with that, it would plague them.
But in the other abscesses accidents in the head other than this one, this is not this chapter, as well as the abscesses that come to the heads of the children and you must the roots of the ears, but the incision of all these is superficial.
And pause the perforation of those from the lower part of them so that the body be relieved of the blood in the lower parts.
And then cure those with what is convenient for that cure.
Chapter .xlii.
Of the incision of scrofulas which occur in the neck.
Many times these abscesses become in the neck and in the armpits and in the groins; and sometimes they occur in the other parts of the body.
And those that occur in the neck, and there are many that are generated among them, and all scrofula of those is within its own tunic, and as in the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have recounted.
And the kinds of these scrofulas are many, because of those there are some stony, and of those there are that contain humidity, and of those are malignant ones which do not obey cure.
Therefore, in that one which you see of good disposition in the Touch, of which the color of that which is manifest is proper to the color of the neck, and is maugre in all parts, and is not annexed to the nerve of the neck, nor to the veins, nor to the artery, and is not tender, then you must incise it with superficial section from the lower part to the upper part of the body from the line of .G. within the line of .B., and scrape it from all parts, and extend the lips of the neck with a scalpel, or with many scalpels if you have need of them, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract it little by little.
And it is more careful that the vein or nerve be not incised.
And let the spatula not be too sharp, that it does not injure your hand while inciding, or that it disturbs the patient, and that you cut only what is necessary to cut; for if you were to cut a vein or artery and you prohibit yourself from your operation, then the wound will stop with vitriol or other powders that stop the flow of blood, and tighten the wound, and leave that within which the sharpness of the abscess remains and the wound is softened and begins to be pus-filled. When the blood is cut.
Therefore, return to your operation while you have completed it.
And then inquire with your little finger if there is any cause of the other small abscesses, therefore cut those and clean them.
And if it is in the root of the large abscess, cover it so that you do not cut that abscess from its root. Cover it so that you place that with a strong bent iron and that you leave it there until it falls by itself without harm.
And then fill the wound with old cotton which you have already submerged in Egyptian ointment, and then cure that.
And if you cut that abscess entirely, then cover it so that you adjust the two lips of the wound and close it as soon as pus comes out so that there is no remaining superfluity.
But if you see that there is superfluity due to the size of the abscess, cover it so that you understand to cut the root of it, and extract it and administer a suture and that which is said.
And those of the abscesses that contain humidity, perforate it with a superficial perforation here where you see the place of maturation of it, and place a perforation of it so that it lets the pus out from the bottom of the body, as we have said.
And then administer a perforation, poultices with ointment and similar things to those, so that it corrodes what is left of the corruption. And then when you see the wound already cleaned, then cure it with ointment of generative flesh until it is healed.
Chapter .xliii.
Of the section of the pile of the abscess that happens within the gullet.
The ancients said this section in the epiglottis, and no one has seen in our land that it has been done.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a hernia, cover that the extraction of the epiglottis be avoided, as for that it is not done well for that all the veins and major arteries of the patient are here.
But in those who have abscesses caused in the mouth or gullet or both ears, when the illness is not in the canal, cover using the section of the epiglottis to avoid the damage which is done by perforation.
Therefore, when we want this, that they cut the epiglottis below three circles of the circles of the epiglottis, or four with a small section for the width in the one that is between two circles by quantity, that the section be in cartilage, not in the flesh, and this place is convenient for section, because it is deprived of flesh and the blood vessels of it are few.
And if the physician is fearful, cover that he extends the throat of the gullet with an incision, and then make the incision until it reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if you see any cause of them.
And then cut the cartilage as we have recommended; and it is signified over the section of the canal by the flame which is of that exit with that which is of it disrupted and by the abscess of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, as the hour is remade in which perforation is feared, add two lips of the throat of the wound, and stitch that alone with the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recounted, the exposition is not but that you see that some of those abscesses have already opened the throat of the patient, and the patient has come into death, and the air of it is contracted, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound by some respiration, and be saved from death.
And for this command to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed; and the malice of it is for three days; and then cover the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And that which I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and put it in her throat and cut with it a part of the canal of the lung, and I was called to the cure of her, and I brought the woman back as she was dying, and I uncovered the wound and brought back the blood which was coming out of the wound small.
Therefore, I was confessed that she had not cut a vein nor guidegi, and the wind was coming out of the wound, and I cured her until she was healed.
And I did not accuse the servant if she did not recover her voice, and after some days she returned to improvement of her dispositions.
And now I say that there is no fear in the section of the epilhot.
Chapter XLIV.
Of the incision on the abscess that occurs in the throat outside, and is called a throat hernia.
This abscess called a throat hernia is a large abscess according to the color of the body, and it moves in women.
And it is in two ways, whether it is natural or accidental.
And in the natural one it is not born to cure.
And the accidental one is in two ways, of which one is similar to fatty nodes, and the other way is similar to an abscess that is made by the blockage of an artery, and in that one there is fear. And no cove that it be presumed to him as iron, but in that one that is small. And then you probe that and investigate that with the finger, and if you find it similar to a fatty node, and it is not suspended by any of the veins, then you incise it as the nodes, and extract it with that which contains it from the skin and the bursa; and if not, then you scrutinize its whole being, and then cure the place with what is necessary for healing before it is healed.
Chapter XLV.
Of the incision of the species of nodes.
Of nodes there are many species, and I have already said all the species of them in the division.
And I have to count thus the difference between a node and an excrescence as if there were a doubt.
Therefore, I say that in an excrescence there is heat and fever and vehement pains until the boiling of the superfluity is subsided; and it is a complication of putrefaction that at the hour ceases the fever, the pain, and the heat.
But in a node there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it counts that which is the lion's head which is in its own sac.
And it is according to the color of the body, and the beginning of it is like a seed and it is made as a vessel, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two species, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of a node, that you probe it and inquire about it at the beginning with the instrument that is called intromes, according to what will come its form in the chapter which is next to this.
And this way of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the moist place which you find in the abscess, and you revolve your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the core.
And then, finally, your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and you extract the intromes and consider what is issued in the trace of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision according to what I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the trace of the intromes there is no humidity, then you know that it is fatty.
And cut over it with an incision having the shape of a cross according to this form: as you have been taught, and suspend it with forceps, and excise the core from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it must be so, and then you extract it in pieces until there remains no cause from it.
For if from it remains no cause, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that from it remains any small part, then complete the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and place over it that which sits abscess caut, and cure it from the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you sew the two lips of it and cure it with that which incarnates.
But if a pulsating vein is in it opposite, or non-pulsating, then you cauterize and moisten the place of zegi trissat that is vitriol and leave that strait for two or three days until you can pierce the wound and that the boiling of the blood rests; and then return to incise that which is broken from the node.

Chapter .xlvii.
Of the cure of the breasts of men which are assembled from women.
Sometimes breasts of certain men become inflamed, like those that begin to be hairy, and then the breasts become inflamed, and the breasts are assembled like those of women, and they are pus-filled, they are removed.
And to him who has this, he must cut those with a lunar section according to this form, from the line of B. to the line of G., and then scrape the entire thickness, and then fill the wound with a medicament of flesh color, and then adjust the two lips of the wound with stitching, and care for him until it is healed.
But if the breast inclines to the sides and is softened by its magnitude as it should to women, then it is cut in two parts, its surpluses, with two sections similar to the lunar figure, of which each one is contained in the other, as long as the major line contains the minor one according to this form of the line of B. and the line of G. And then scrape the flesh which is between the two lips of the wound, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said of the suture and the powders, what is necessary in the cure until it is healed.
And if you do not comply with the incision of this one that must be cut because of the restlessness of the patient, and the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with a cloth submerged in corrosive liquid and leave it until that corrosive one that is the flesh, and then care for him until it is healed.
Chapter .xlviii.
Of the perforation of abscesses that come from the nipple.
These abscesses that come from the nipple are of the kind of scrofulas, hard, which contain a skin that is removed.
And of those, some contain humidity; and those that contain humidity must be incised with a lunar section according to this figure: from the line of G. to the line of B. And as soon as everything that is in the abscess of the healthy is evacuated, then you fill it with old cloth and leave it until the next day.
And then the cloth is removed and it is cured with a suitable ointment to it, until it is healed.
And if the abscess is of the kind of nodes and scrofulas, then you cut it as we have said in the section on scrofulas similarly.
But if the wound is extended so that it is a pockmark, then administer cauterizing in it according to what we have said before.
Chapter .xlix.
Of the incision of abscesses that occur because of an artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the flesh which is over it is consolidated, then many times abscesses occur. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are from the artery or vein: that when the abscess is from the artery it is long aggregated in the front of the body; and that when you pierce the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it a kind of stridor.
And that one which is from the vein is red and manifest on the front of the body.
And incision over this abscess is an error, and most of all in those that are from the armpits, and the corners, and the neck, and many other places of the body; and it is very large, so that its cure with iron should be avoided, and that one which is in the extremities, or on the head, should be avoided.
But over that one which is from the inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut in the flesh a long section; and then probe the section with a probe and the artery, and deliver from the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then put on that needle and make it penetrate into the other part, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which cause you to see in the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then poke the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula until all the blood that is in it is removed, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer a cure in which it is generated power until the ligaments fall; and then care for it with suitable ointments to it until it is healed.
And if the abscess is from the section of a vein, then you must have with your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the flesh, and then introduce the needle from the place which you have had from your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract it from the other part, and then tie the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you in the ligament of the grape of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the thread with that needle from all the abscess, besides the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle of it until when it is issued the water that is in it, then you cut the superfluity of the flesh, and leave what of it is tied.
And then place on it the powder which you have submerged in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with poultices and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which occurs due to a twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and similarly abscesses occur in nerves when they are struck or when they are overworked, and similarly.
And it is made most in the places of the helpers or the heel, or in any place where the joints are sore.
And it is a serious abscess, and it is assembled to the color of the other body, and in the major parts of it dispositions are seen, and when it is tightened with violence, the patient feels in it a seeming stupor.
And it is not an abscess added in the front of the body, and for that it is left the code, and it is sore to all parts and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore, those that are in the joints should not be treated with iron, because it will certainly cause a contraction.
But the one that is in the head or in the front, treat it with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then take that with the forceps and cut it to the root.
And if it is large, then you suspend it with a hook, and excise it, and then you cover it; and adjust the wound with suture, and cure it until it is healed.
Chapter 2.
Of the section of an abscess which occurs from a boil that occurs to the belly.
And it happens to some men, growths in the bellies of those and in other parts of the body of those, which are called fungals because of their similarity to fungi, of which the root is subtle and the head of it is thick; and already the lips of those are converted, and it is of those that are small, and it is of those that are magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him were two parts which were more like fungi, and there was no difference between those white, of fine root.
And already the lips of those were reversed and they were splitting, and humidity was running from it all the time.
Therefore, I incised those and brought out in one of them about eighteen inches. and the other about six inches.
And the operation in the incision of them is that you consider, then if the patient is humid, and the color of the boil is white, humid, of subtle root; then you should cut it with a spatula, and be in your presence cauterize it with fire, because many times the secretion of it must be expelled with much blood; and if you come to the blood, cauterize it.
And if you see the patient pale and fearful, guard yourself from incision with iron; but then take a piece of recent lead made, and strengthen it with that boil, the manner of which is that we have said; and leave it there for two days.
And then adjust in the stricture of the lead wire; therefore, do not cease to strengthen the lead greatly, until it is excised and falls by itself with its work.
But if the boil is of a thick root, then in the incision of it there is some cause of fear and of terror, and more so in the one that is in the belly.
But it is possible that you should cut most of it, and then cauterize it so that it does not return.
And then cure it until the wound is healed.

And the minister has those of two parts or be tied in the sheet so that the body of him does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother with humid oil and mucilage of althea and fennel and seed of lily.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then introduces her hand with facility into the mother, and then seeks with the hand in the place where the forceps are in the fetus.
And convenient places in this: therefore you consider if the fetus is prepared that descends upon its head, and then you place the forceps in the heels of it, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or even the beard, or in the fork of it, or in the proper places of the back, or even the hypochondria.
But if the descent is upon the feet of it, then in the penile, or in the middle of the back.
And consider that you have the forceps with your right hand, and pause the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of your left hand, and introduce the hand with facility and place the forceps in one of those places which we have said, until you arrive at the left cause.
And then pause and place in the position of it another forceps, or the third if it is necessary, so that the traction be equal, and not be extension according to its rectitude only.
And be careful to every part, so that the emission of it be alleviated as it is done in the time of the eradication of it.
And consider in it that which is between them that the extension be mollified; and if any part of it is retained, then consider that the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and introduces them with skill and revolves with those that are retained.
Therefore if the part of the fetus is outside, then the forceps are changed into the place which is more out; and do so until all the fetus is outside.
But if the hand is outside the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by the constriction of it, then consider that a cloth be enveloped over it; and then extract it until all is outside, and incise it either in the junction of the hand or in the groin.
And so consider that you do in the other hand and in the two feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or happens to it constriction in the emission, or is in the head of it water adjusted, then consider that you introduce between the fingers the spine and split the head and extract the water, or what discards this with an instrument which is called "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which is next to this.
And similarly do if the fetus is of large head by nature: and then consider that you incise it with the algematu, or that you press it with the alunda as we have said; and then extract the bones with the forceps.
And if the head is outside and is constricted by the fork, then it is split until the humidity which is in the feet is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obeys to emission, then you incise the head as soon as it is possible to you.
And if the remains of the womb are apostate or are in it hydrophic, then consider that you perforate it until the running of the humidity that is in it.
But if the fetus is upon its feet, then the traction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the mother is lighter.
But if it is constricted by the belly and the feet, then consider that you extract that with the cloth which you will have enveloped over your hand, and that you make the belly and the feet until the water runs out of those.
But if the other limbs are still and the head turns, then the midwife inserts her left hand; but if the mother's mouth is open, then she inserts her hand into the perineum of the woman, and with that she takes the head, and pulls it into the mouth of the mother, and then inserts a hook, or two hooks, and pulls it with those.
And if the mother's mouth is constricted by an abscess, cauterize the one that occurs to the woman; then cover it so that it is not touched; rather, administer an infusion of humid fatty causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on the side, then if possible, it should be pricked; and administer the water that we have said in the living fetus.
And if that is not possible, then it should be incised in pieces, and extracted.
And make sure that you leave no cause of the second birth.
And when you have completed the entire operation, then administer the water that we have said for the cure of the cauterizations that occur to the mother.
And if there is a flow of blood, then send them down in styptic waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in whose belly there was a dead fetus, and then, on that very same fire, another pregnancy, and then, on that same fire, the fetus is another. It happened to a woman a long time ago an abscess in her navel; and it inflated so much that it opened, and began to throw out pus.
And I was called to the cure of it, and medicated it for a long time, and the plague did not consolidate.
Then I placed on it some causes of a strong plaster, and extracted a bone from it, and after a few days, I extracted another bone; and I was very amazed, as there were no bones in the belly.
And then I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore, I continued to treat the abscess, and extracted more bones from it, the woman existing in her usual dispositions, and already living in that manner for a long time, cured of it a little bit of pus.
And I do not affirm that it was strange, but that in this there is science and help to what the doctor artifices with his hand for cure administers.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of the forceps with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of the spreader in which the blades are joined, to which joining there are two forceps at the two extremities of two blades. But however, this forceps should be more subtle than the spreader, and be made either of ebony or of a branch of beech.
And let the width of each shaft be two fingers, and the margin of each be one finger, and the length of each is a palm and a half; and in the middle place of the two shafts are two adjustments of that same shaft, which are already fastened, of which the length is the majority of a palm and a little more, and the width of each is two fingers, or a little less.
And these two attachments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it may be opened with those when you revolve the two prescribed forceps.
Another form similar to that more subtle and lighter:
It is made of ebony or beech shafts according to the resemblance of forceps. But however, at the extremity of it there are two attachments as seen, and the length of those attachments is about a palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And as you want to open the mother with those, then you make the woman lie on the litter with her feet hanging down, opening what is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, equally according to the quantity that you want of the opening of the mouth of the mother until the midwife makes sure that you want.

Form of the amisidat2 with which the large head is contained
And it is assembled like forceps with teeth at the extremity, as seen, and sometimes it is made long as forceps according to this form, as seen, to which there are teeth as teeth of a saw with which it is incised and contained. Form of the amisidat a little:
Form of an unci having a spine:
Form of an unci having two spines:
Form of a spatum having two extremities with which the head is cut off:
Form of two broad spatums:
All those instruments are exercised, and when they are multiplied the species of it and are prepared, the artificer, as much as is lighter to his operation and as much as is more convenient for men by their quantity.
And do not use those instruments, no matter what, because the need for them is not excusable.
Of the extraction of the second.
When the second is retained, the enfantament should be commanded, so that you command the patient to retain their breath, and then make that stornudar, and strengthen your hand over the mouth of it and over the nostrils of it, and if by this it is expelled, it is good.
And if not, then you take a cloth and perforate in the cover a hole and put in it herbs inside the mouth of the mother, such as calament and rue and aneth and chamomile and siccated arabic and cassia lignea and santaurea. All these herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the cloth, and put that over the fire.
And then put a straw of cane in the mouth of the mother, and keep that inside so that the vapor comes to the cavity of the mother.
And then make that stornudar as we have said, and the second is expelled with speed.
But if this cure remains and it is not expelled, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a mixture of althea, and then introduce that into the cone and seek the second with that, and as she has found it, then take it and extend it little by little. But if it is annexed in the perineum of the mother, then introduce her hand as we have recounted, and when she has found the second, extract it little by little, according to rectum, so that the mother does not feel the traction violently. It should be changed to the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, we have already recounted the cure with sturnutation and with medication of the cloth with herbs.
But if it is not expelled with all the causes which we have recounted, then guard that you do not tire on that in iteration of abstraction, but rather that what is expelled from it to the mouth of the mother lies to the cloth of the woman, and then christenize that with enguent and tetrafarmacon; because that will make it soften and after a few days it will be dissolved and expelled.
But when it may be possible, it is of it elevated bad odor to the head, and to the stomach, and that leads the patient; and therefore it should be administered sub-fumiguacios and conveniences to that.
But some of the Ancients already know sub-fumigacio of nazitort and of dried figs.
Form of instrument with which the woman is sub-fumigated should the retention of menses and of the second:
It should be made of silver or of brass.
And it should be placed the fine extremity in the cone and the wide extremity over the fire, and the sub-fumigacio should be placed over the embers of the fire.
And keep that inside so that the sub-fumigacio is consumed and iterate another.
Of cure of the unperforated infant's anus.
Many infants are born and the anus of them is not perforated, the ones which already have a subtle and opilated cicatrix. Therefore, it should be commanded to the midwife to perforate with her finger that cicatrix; and if not, perforate that with a sharp spatum, and guard that it does not touch the sphincter.
And then place on that wool infused in wine and oil; and then cure that with enguent until it is healed.
But if you fear that it will be opilated, then place in the hole a straw for many days, and remove it when the child will want to swallow.
And already accidents oppilation of the anus by consolidation of plaque or of abscess; therefore it should be commanded that that consolidation be incised, and then be cured with that which we have said of the cure and of the lead.
Of cure of the fistulas that develop from the anus.
The fistulas that develop in the parting of the anus pus low node and thickness the ones which develop near the anus outside or in the space of the one parting.
And it is a fistula or many.
And as that node is antiquated and runs of the humid whey white or subtle puss, and some times from these fistulas some penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by that which is expelled from them by the egress and by windiness; and some times use the patient of egress, and forth leu is expelled from them worms.
And from these fistulas some times in the space penetrate into the bladder, and into the meat of the vagina; and from these penetrate into the junction of the thigh and into the knot of the hip.
And that in which is known fistula penetrating into the anus and not penetrating, is that you put your finger inside the anus, and introduce a subtle tenta of brass or of iron into the fistula when there is no turtuosity.
But if in that there is turtuosity, then introduce into that a subtle tenta of lead or of horse hair until you feel the tenta or the hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel any of that, nor do you notice any cause of digestion, worms, or flatulence, as we have said, then you should know that it is non-penetrating, and therefore you turn to the cure.
And when the fistula penetrates into the bladder or into the meat of the vagina, then the meaning of it is the emission of urine from that and prohibition of it so that the place with medicine may be consolidated.
But if it penetrates into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the circulation, then the sign of it is that the fistulous opening penetrates here, if there is no tumor inside the bone, and pain in the circulation of the limb; and that from it pus always flows; and that in that medicine, it is not cured, nor is it consolidated by rinsing.
And in all those fistulas penetrating there is no cure of all, and the cure of those is the toil and vanity of the medical leaves on which it is based.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is expected according to what I have told you, and what I have already proven.
And it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back and elevates his legs into them, the thighs being inclined towards his belly, and then introduce a probe of lead, or of iron if there is a tumor in the fistula, until you know the place where the probe goes.
And if the patient feels the probe around the buttock, then you cover with your hand the buttock.
And if you feel in your hand the probe already by itself penetrating, or another that you feel between your hand and that skin or flesh, then you know certainly that it is penetrating; and therefore do not work on that, because it is not in that healing, as we have said.
But however, some say that it is cured in some men tart.
And of the medicine by which help is expected in it is that you ignite a cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as it is preceded, and introduce that ignited one into the fistula until it reaches around the buttock; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those carns adjusted to the fistula have been cauterized, which are similar to the feather quill of a bird.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border until all those carns that are cauterized can be covered, and then cure that with medicines the flesh engendering and consolidating, and if it is healed, well is; and if not, then it is not healed in any time by other cure.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate into your hand which is in the buttock, and between that and the probe which is always a space of flesh or of skin, and sometimes the fistula in that which is the surface of the buttock, then dry the buttock from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying with the probe, and it is in the fistula until the drying reaches the place where the extremity of the probe reaches, and by the probe it is liberated and catched.
And then purify those carns that are assembled like the feather quill of a bird and do not break from any of them.
But if flow of blood sometimes comes between you and your operation when you are inserting those carns, then the best that may be and of the lighter pus instrument is to cauterize with fire or with acute medicine, because cauterizing with fire adjusts good two habits: it is the cauterization of those carns adjusted, and abscess of the blood excretion of the humidities.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border or in a caul of tripe until the place gets a brace, and then cure the plague with rinses of hard flesh engendering and consolidating.
And so medicines in which there is styptication and excretion; when then it is restored it is already healed and you fear no iteration.
But if the fistula already reaches into the perineum of the buttock and is elongated from it to the surface of the body, then introduce your hand into the buttock and inquire with that.
And therefore if you feel the probe and between you and it is always a space of skin or flesh, and it is proper to penetration, then it is not an operation on it but according to my advice and of hope.
Which cause is to administer in it one of three ways: or that you cauterize it as we have said; or that you dry it until you obtain the concavity of it so that it is possible for you to introduce your fingers and the proper cure; and do not proceed with a cut so that you do not injure the sphincter containing the buttock, and that occurs on the patient as a result of the digestion of its will; and then cure that with what we have said, because it is very strong if it heals; or that you elongate that veil and cleanse that pus that dries that inside the buttock, as we have said, or with a probe or with another instrument of sharp extremity, and then purify those carns that are in the section within which you can make a perforation; and then strive to make the restoration of the whole plague with section, and if the orifice of pus above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the part of the buttock, and pus light flows from the patient. And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: it is when you introduce the probe into the fistula, and it is in the latz of the buttock around the surface of the body with the buttock and on the margin of the buttock, then take a probe of perforated extremity, which is as if a needle for preparing the hearts according to this form:
And within that faithful envelope of v fibers or around those; and then try to introduce a thread into the fistula until you achieve its cavity.
But if it penetrates into the edge of the anus, then you extract the thread from that tract so that you introduce your finger into the anus; and extract the end of the thread and adjust the two ends simultaneously, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or two, and when you have incised the thread more deeply into the flesh, tighten it well so that those flesh which are between the two ends of the thread and which are closing.
And then care for the plague until it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate, in whatever manner it is prepared for you, so that it is moved in the preon, because it is not for you to do this so that you do not cut the skin; and then do it until it is healed.
The shape of the spatum spinos with which the fistula is cut: the curvature of which is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that you do not cut what is not necessary, as sometimes happens.
Of suturing hemorrhoids in which blood runs in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are in two manners, because they are between the anus like that which is of cartilage, or those which are like the fat of a ram. And of those there are small and large, and that blood runs from those always and is one, and they are many, and they are outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
But however, those that are outside the anus are according to the few humidity, of which water citrina or a little blood with a continuous body runs, and they are according to the color of the body.
And the cure of that which is inside the anus is that you command the patient to squat and to press until the anus is open and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take and suspend with hooks or whatever you have those with your nail, and then cut those by their roots.
But if the hooks are not held in those by the humidity of them and their softening, then take those with rough cloth or with a stick or with wool fleece, and extract those with your fingers, and then cut those and pulverize on them some powders caudas near the incision, so that they are applied to those in place of cauterization; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter of cauterization. And then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey egressio, then christenize the patient with a cristeri in which there is a small bite, and wash it with that water that is in the anus and that obeys egressio slightly when the patient squeezes.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of them is slight, and it is that you take those with your nail, or whatever you take those with a hook, and cut those, and then cure those with the water that we have said until they are healed.
And that which you have incised, cover that you administer suture of them according to this manner: take thread enveloped and introduce that into a needle and then extract the hemorrhoids to the upper parts, and make that penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and envelop the two ends of the thread in the part further from the needle, and it is laterally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with a strong structure, and then cut the thread and extract the needle.
And do this to all, and leave one of those untied, so that the superfluity of blood runs from that one.
And then place on the anus cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerot; and place that on the anus and command the patient to rest. And then leave that until it closes; and when it is closed, cure those with ointments or with other cure until it is healed.
And as they are old and no longer work in that medicine, then you must cut those with the point of a spatum or with your nail until they are made moist and the pus of those is extracted, which prohibits those from consolidation; and then cure those until they are consolidated.
Then you must remove those with a sharp pus vehemently that the first one until it bleeds and is excoriated; and then cure those until they are healed.
Know that almesamir, it is called, and it is not if not a red knot according to the color of the body resembling a head of a clavicle, and it is made in all the body and most in the parts below the feet and in the fingers, and it must be due to those pains the ailment.
And therefore, whoever it is incised that which is in the circuit of the claw, and it is held with the forceps or with a hook, and it is eradicated from its root; and then cure that.
And if you wish, cauterize the second one that is preceded in its chapter.
More than a wart is a small, rough, fistulous, round eminence on the surface of the body, and many times they appear on the hands of children.
And the cure for it is that you extend and cut into it, or that you tighten it with a thread or by sewing it up. And if you wish, cauterize it, as we have said, with fire or with a sharp medicine.
But a nettle is a small, fetid or fistulous eminence on the surface of the body that goes into the skin, and when the sting finds it, it is felt in it like a bite of a nettle, and it is made around the body.
And the cure for it is that you take a feather quill of eagle or of vulture, and it be strong, and place that over the nettle inside while containing the circle of the quill with the parts of it; and then revolve your hand with the quill inside while cutting that which is in the circuit of the nettle, and place that in the skin of the flesh, and that you eradicate the nettle from its root.
And if you wish, do it with a quill of iron or of steel according to this form:
Let the part above the quill be drawn to a subtlety, blunt (so it is not perforated), enveloped so that over the said one the apprehension of it be abviated and the revolution of it.
And if you wish, cauterize the nettle according to what is said before in the cauterization of a boil in the chapter of cauterization.
Of the form of the instruments that are administered to give christening.
Sometimes christenings are made of silver or of lead or of iron melted or hammered; and sometimes they are made of those instruments small and large according to those to which they are administered, because that which is administered in the cure of the little children be small; and of those whose hips are sore or painful, the christenings of those be small.
The form of a large and few christening:
The head of the quill of it above in which the pouch is tied be wide according to this manner; and be to it the distinction the one in which the pouch is tied thus as times.
And the extremity of it further down, the one which is inserted into the anus, be blunt (so it is not open) much lion, drawn to a subtlety; and in one of the sides of it be two holes, and in the other side one hole, and be the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays and a little thicker one a little.
And be the pouch in which be placed the medicines of bladder of beast or of sheepskin, and the root of it be a palm.
And be perforated by many holes as it is revolved; and if the space which is between the holes the thickness of the finger.
And then insert into those holes a strong thread of cru thread which be of ten threads, or about those; and adjust with it the pouch; and when it is placed in it the pouch, be straight in the head of the christening between two distinct ones with strong constriction, and then cauterize with it each hole: But the quality of cauterizing with it is that you fill the pouch with the medicine, which be warmed according to the quantity of the tolerance of the patient; and guard yourself that it be not too hot nor too cold.
And then the patient be laid on his back, and elevate his legs up and place beneath him a cushion on which already are the men or a bolster; and then anoint the extremity of the cauterizer with oil or with album of egg or with mucilage of fenugreek or of similar; and then insert that into the anus with facility, and then the minister takes the pouch and expresses that with two hands and at the same time with vehemence until it be evacuated into the bowel all that which is in the christening; and then extract the christening and the patient raises his legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces that as an easement, have it as much as it can; and if sleep with it for a whole night, it is more beneficial in recovery.
But if you cauterize that in the diseases of solution of belly and the easement of it the cure, then you iterate the cauterizer until it be healed.
And if in the anus be hemorrhoids or abscesses leading, then be the christening much subtle and lion, of the christenings with which the children are christened.
Of the cure of the plagues.
I have already said in the division of the cure of the plagues what was convenient to the book, and I say thus the cure of those with my and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that the plagues are diversified according to what in which they are made the plagues and according to the place upon which befall the plagues.
And the causes for which many times are made the plagues are as such as a wound of spear, or incision of sword or of axe, or percussion with lance, or with clubs, or with arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the places of the body are as such as a plague which befalls upon the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the arm, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I am recounting the cure of some diseases so that you may apply that reasoning and rule to other diseases.
And I will begin with the diseases of the head, for the remembrance of the composite ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple disease occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is from a blow or a similar injury, and the vein has been squeezed so much that it is a large wound and you fear that the patient may have an abscess, then you should immediately take care and perform a cephalic phlebotomy, and do not delay this; and extract from that blood according to the quantity of its virtue, if no other cause prevents phlebotomy, especially if the blood that is extracted from the wound is little.
And it should be phlebotomy on the opposite side of the diseased area; and guard the patient from repletion and from wine and from heavy foods.
But if any cause prohibits phlebotomy, then lessen the food and do not approach meat or wine.
And place on the wound, if a boil occurs, a poultice infused in rose oil or in wine in which is stippled.
But if it is certain that a boil will occur, then place on the wound, if it is recent, its own blood and the air has not yet changed that powder which I will recount shortly.
And if the air has already changed that, then place on it an ointment until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or is from a deep cut and the lips of it are not adjusted with pins, then adjust those with suture according to what I will recount of the suturing of them.
But if the wound is already uncovered of the bone and tendon, and there is no retention of it but a small suspension, then incise that and then treat the wound with medicines and restore the flesh in the place of the vein, and command the patient to be sparing of foods in which there is grease: caps and forms cooked and similar to them, until it is composed.
And if a putrefaction occurs in the vein and it does not adhere to the bone, then you incise all that pus and cast it out, and then treat that.
But if in these wounds the artery or vein from which blood can flow is involved, and it is not severed by medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find it not incised, then you incise it with a spatula, or cauterize it; and if necessity provokes that what we have said does not confer, then you cauterize it until the blood is severed.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is lighter; in this way that you pulverize on them this powder, which consolidated before the air changes them.
And the manner of the powder is this: receive olive oil, one part, dragon's blood, two parts, and cauterized earth, three parts; all be ground and sifted, and of this fill the wound, and be constrained by good constriction until it well adheres on it, and be coagulated with the blood.
And then strengthens that with pins and loosens it, and do not untie it while it is thus that it is not suppurated, for it is not eradicated from it the medicine until it is healed.
And sometimes you do this alone cauterization, when you do not have in present olive oil and dragon's blood.
And already you do this same operation in the great wounds when it convenes that it be placed on them and be tightened, and wounds recent with their blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summer time, then it is not understood in the position of this powder, but then treat those with what we have said, in this way that you place on them some digested ointments, or that you place on them powder of barley flour with water and honey until they obtain a poultice; and then treat those with the other cure until they are healed.
But if a fracture occurs with the wound in bone, and it is small, then you extract it with a tool.
And I will say the cure of the fractures of the head in that which is venomous.
Of the wounds of the neck.
But if the wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in medication, and between the wound of the head when it is simple.
But if already the nerve of the neck is incised or the artery, then if it is the nerve, it is not in it to be cured but that its cure be avoided with what makes vehement astringency, such as ziniar and zegi that is vitriol and similar to them for that it is noxious to the nerves and contracts it. And do not place on the wound any cause of all cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the most delicate of all the members.
And if it is cured with medicines lighter, such as it is washed with sweet water, some herbs infused in rose or un-rose oil, and then when it is washed with sweet water and the other smaller herbs according to this manner, and humid ointments.
But if the plague is large, then administer suture, or shorten the lips of it, and then care for it with powders until it is healed.
But if the plague is deep or an accident occurs in it at the lower part of the wound, then perforate it at the most depressed location.
But if in the plague an artery has already been incised and there is a flow of blood, then separate or dry it, or tie it, or cauterize it if necessary to stop the bleeding.
But if the spinal cord of the neck or all of it has already been incised, and the veins of the neck are saved, then you adjust the lips of the wound with suture over the canal of the neck and do not touch it; raise it and return it to its natural shape, and then strengthen it with a decent structure, and leave it for a few days; and then care for it with ointments in which there is astringency and excitation until it is healed.
But if the plague has already been made in the bone, then strike it, and if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all that you can of them; and what you cannot remove, leave it until the plague is softened, and it is separated, and the discharge from it is relieved.

Of the cure of zechem and fistula.
Know that every plague and abscess when it is inflamed and becomes old, and is made an ulcer, and is not consolidated and throws out pus all the time and is not cut off, then, in whatever member it may be, universally it is called a fistula and we call that azukem.
And a fistula according to truth is a fetid, hard, white nodule, with which there is no pain and to which the concavity is as it is the concavity of the bone of a bird; and for this reason, that is called by some rizatz, that is, bone.
And it is in some men humid, which throws out pus; and very soon the humidity is cut off in some hours. And some times this humidity is moved, and is little, and is thick, and is subtle.
I have already shown all those causes, and their signs and the cure of them with medicines in the division.
And it is necessary that I make to you know the cure of fistula which is done by way of operation with a knife.
And know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for some of them reach the great veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the head, or the intestines, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or any of the vertebrae of the spine, or any of the joints composed by composition so that of the hand and the foot; and those that give to it proximity of the principal member and of semblance.
And therefore of these fistulas that are according to this manner are of the diseases of difficult healing, and no receive cure, and occupation with that is work and ignorance.
And if it is of the fistulas any the depth of which does not reach these places that have been said, and you wait and trust in the cure of it, and you want to come to knowledge of it, then take the attempt of a probe or of iron, and if the fistula goes according to rectum, and inquire that with it.
But if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate that with a probe of subtle lead, for lead with the lightness of its body is alleviated and curved of the tortuosity.
And if the fistula is having many horrific things, it is not to you possible that you signify upon it with a probe.
Therefore, cleanse the orifice with its orifices, for the moisture by which you cleanse it must go to the other orifices and flow from them.

Of the cure of the intestines and the quality of clysterization with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it makes a collection of pus, and then it is broken and perforated, and pus is ejected from it, and the place remains hollow as if it were a vessel, and the skin that is above it is as fine cloth, and it has not reached the back corruption, and it has not imprinted on the bone or on the nerves or on the ligament, it is called a sinus, and it is not called a fistula.
But however, if the space is prolonged until the corruption presses into some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the cure of it is that the skin is incised entirely as it is turned, and most importantly when it is fine and made like cloth, and so that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin will adhere and that that corruption has not achieved a further consequence, and in the skin there has passed through from the front, then you cure that with clysters.
And it is that you consider the sinus, and then if it is large, and the brac that you see is of a fetid odor, then you clysterize that with an Egyptian medicine which is of oil and strong wine and cumin receiving equal parts, and they are put into a vessel, and they are boiled over the fire until the medicine becomes thick and reaches the consistency of honey.
And then you take from it what is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and clysterize with that the sinus, and strengthen the orifice of it, and leave the medicine in it for the quantity of two hours.
And then you extract that with a spoon; and do this for as many days until the sinus is purified and the stench is removed.
And sometimes it is clysterized with ash water, when this medicine is not present to you; and it is that you take the ash of beech, and put water on it; and then you strain that and clysterize with it until you confess that the sinus is then healed.
And if the patient has no tolerance on the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then clysterize that with water and honey and a little crushed cumin, and clysterize that with wine and honey mixed, because of the property of honey is that it purifies and washes, and the wine makes the sinus adhere, and especially when in the wine there is an excess of astringency and dryness.
And as you do this sometimes and you confess that the sinus is already healed, then clysterize that with water that makes flesh grow in it.
And it is that you take of enguent dyaphinicon and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine; or that you clysterize with it some medicines and other enguents that have the properties which I have already written in the treatise of enguents.

And similarly if the orifice is wide, then you add the lips of it with suture and leave it in the quantity in which between the clyster there is addition.
And if the patient's orifice from which the arm comes out is elevated to the upper parts, then dry that in the lowest place that is in it so that the arm runs inside, because when the arm is compressed in the prepondency of the sinew the flesh is engendered in it.

But that which is over the orifice of the sinew, which you remove every hour so that what is adjusted in it of the arm may escape. And so that you know if what runs from the arm is much or little, or is digested, or is not digested.

Of the cure of panari and nails rubbed and incision of the finger added and section.
Panari is an abscess that arises from under the nail of the finger of the hand or of the foot, and often arises in the other fingers, and as it is prolonged and its cure is less valued, or is an abscess of abscess caut, or is corrupted, and throws out arm until it corrodes the root of the nail, and often corrupts that whole, and often pervades its corruption to the bone until it is a fetid odor, and is made the extremity of the finger lad, and the color of it is made dusky.
And therefore when you will have that with the water that we have said in the division and do not mix your cure, then cover that you cut with iron all the superfluity that is remaining from the nail and then cauterize the wound with water, because cauterization much is helpful in that.
But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, and the additions of the nail void already comprehend the flesh to the parts of the finger, and they begin to sting it and leave it that, then cover that you place a fine ray under the angle of the nail that stings the flesh, and impel it up and cut it with facility, and place over that which remains of the flesh of the medicines comburent corrosive until it be all removed; and then cure it with rinsing until it be healed.

And if you see the corrosion and corruption going into the wound, then you cut it in one of the nuts according to how it is pressed its memory, and then care for it while it is healing.

But this adjusted flesh, which is born in the hands of some men, is very strong in the flesh, and very strong in the bones, or very strong in the nail.

Of incisions of vices, they are varicose.

Of the section above the ailment.
This illness is called nafir in our land, and it is pain that comes in certain limbs, and then it is changed from limb to limb.
And I have already seen that as I will tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and I uncovered her arm and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm, and because it was removed for an hour, I saw that inflammation go as if a worm was climbing, but more lightly than being carried, as if it were living silver when it runs from place to place.
And then it went to the pain of that place and settled in the muscle, and then it stayed there for an hour.
And then it moved to the other side of the body until it reached the other arm.
And then I recommended to myself that I should turn it over all over her body as I had seen; and it was too marvelous of the mutation of it and the velocity of limb to limb. And I had already seen this before in my own veins in that manner, however, I have seen many who felt pain being changed from limb to limb. But I did not see this in the veins as in the woman.
And I did not think it to be otherwise than that because the woman was old, on so of dry body and of uncovered veins, and in this appearance felt that windiness mutated.
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this retro-cure in those who are delicate and with humid bodies of well-closed veins.

Of the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are diversified according to the species, and according to the places of the body in which they are shot, for their diversity is that of those that have large points, and small, and concave, and blunt, so they are solid; and of those that have three angles, and of those that have tongues; and of those that have shafts.
And of the signs of the neck is when it hits in it an arrow, and passes through the bone, and it is issued from the cyph, which is above the brain, for it is violently shaken, and scotomia, and vertigo, and rumble in the legs, and inflammation and rumble of the tongue, and spasm and mixing of understanding and vomiting of bile, and very much is cut off the word and destroyed the voice, and it is issued from the place of the plague white humidity resembling powder, and eyes of it resembling the fluidity of the flesh.
And therefore if these signs appear to you, then you abstain from the cure and the extraction of the arrow, if it is not outside.
But the signs of the arrow when it hits the heart, are that it is near the left nipple, and feels with that which it is stuck in a hard cause, and it is not a void cause; and very much the movement of the arrow is similar to the movement of the hand, and running of the plague black blood, and it seizes that coldness of the extremities, and a sore cold, and syncope; and therefore know that death descends upon it all at once.
And the signs when the arrow has wounded the lung, so are the spitting of phlegm of blood from the plague, and the vessels that are near the neck are inflamed, and the color of the patient is changed, and he exhales great spirit, and demands the extraction of cold air.
And if it hits the arrow in the ligament which is in the foot, and the pain then is near the small of the back, and it is made the leg great with vehement pain and with sigh, and it is not bad all the limbs of the muscles.
And if it hits the arrow in the stomach, then very much the eyes of the plague are seen with some indigested food.
And if it hits the arrow in the belly, and it is stuck in it, eyes some wound of the plague, or the web, or the intestine which is disrupted, and there is no hope in the cure of it extraction of the arrow.
And if the arrow hits the bladder, and it is issued from it urine, and it processes from it some cause to the parts outside, and very much is pain upon the patient, then you know that it is mortal.
May the other members, as well as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, and assistants, and the vertebrae of the back, and the clavicle, and the thigh, and the leg, and their likeness of the limbs, be saved according to the major dispositions when the arrow does not strike a vein or artery and is not a poisonous arrow.

And I saw a woman to whom an arrow was shot in her belly, and the plague was consolidated from within her, and it was not changed in her dispositions in any way, and the woman did not suffer harm in any of her natural operations.

Of phlebotomy of the veins.

Of ventosa and the qualities of using them.
Ventozas are of horns, or of iron, or of lead.
And ventosa is made in two ways: one of them is with scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is ventosa without scarification.
And this ventosa that is without scarification is in two ways, whether it is with fire or without fire.
And to the ventosa that are administered with scarification and extraction of blood there are fourteen locations of the body, of which one in which ventosa are placed is the occiput, and it is the rear part of the head; and the middle place of the two parts of the neck together; and ventosa of the chin below the jawbone below the mouth; and ventosa of the two shoulder blades; and ventosa of the alohoster, and it is above the end of the rib; and ventosa of the two armpits; and ventosa of the two groins.
And ventosa does not extract the blood but from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not catch the virtue by those, as it is caught by phlebotomy; nor is it advisable that ventosa be made with fire or without fire in any disease caused by repletion until the whole body is evacuated.
But if necessity provokes ventosa for disease or for continuous, administer it at all times at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle of it and in any time that it is.
And therefore when times in any of those causes, and properly if it is in the third or middle of the month, then command ventosa to be made more than it is passed from the day of two or three hours.
And the benefit of ventosa of the neck is that when that confers gravity to the head and ad that which is poured into the eyes; but it is advisable that that be after evacuation of the whole body.
And this ventosa is in the location of phlebotomy of the cephalic.
And it is not light that use of it that one that is of frega complexion, or in the one that is catarr, for it gives to that great damage.
And therefore it is not advisable to use it for the elderly, and in those whose heads are of cold diseases.
But to him that over that is continuing over it is made oblivion; and therefore it is advisable that you command the ventosa to pause his hand a little with the ventosa to the parts below, fearing the generation of oblivion.

And if we want the extraction of much blood, we scarify with much scarification; and if we knew that the blood was thick, then we should scarify with a pre-existing scarification.
And the term of scarification in which is the depth of the incision, only.
And if that one whose incision is thick, hard, dark, and whose pores are narrow, then the places of the ventilators should be anointed more gently, more open, more resolved; if it is in summer, like olive oil of aloes or olive oil of violets, or olive oil of two almonds, or olive oil of fig; and if it is in winter, then narcissus oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or of the same kind.
